<a href="/wiki/NFPA_704#Yellow" title="NFPA 704"><span style="color:black;" title="Reactivity code 0: Normally stable, even under fire exposure conditions, and is not reactive with water. E.g., liquid nitrogen">0</span></a></div></div></div></div>
</td></tr>




</tbody></table>
<p>Manganese compounds are less toxic than those of other widespread metals, such as <a href="/wiki/Nickel" title="Nickel">nickel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> However, exposure to manganese dusts and fumes should not exceed the ceiling value of 5&#160;mg/m<sup>3</sup> even for short periods because of its toxicity level.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>  Manganese poisoning has been linked to impaired motor skills and cognitive disorders.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The permanganate exhibits a higher toxicity than the manganese(II) compounds. The fatal dose is about 10&#160;g, and several fatal intoxications have occurred. The strong oxidative effect leads to <a href="/wiki/Necrosis" title="Necrosis">necrosis</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Mucous_membrane" title="Mucous membrane">mucous membrane</a>. For example, the <a href="/wiki/Esophagus" title="Esophagus">esophagus</a> is affected if the permanganate is swallowed. Only a limited amount is absorbed by the intestines, but this small amount shows severe effects on the kidneys and on the liver.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Manganese exposure in <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> is regulated by the <a href="/wiki/Occupational_Safety_and_Health_Administration" title="Occupational Safety and Health Administration">Occupational Safety and Health Administration</a> (OSHA).<sup id="cite_ref-osha.gov_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osha.gov-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> People can be exposed to manganese in the workplace by breathing it in or swallowing it. OSHA has set the legal limit (<a href="/wiki/Permissible_exposure_limit" title="Permissible exposure limit">permissible exposure limit</a>) for manganese exposure in the workplace as 5&#160;mg/m<sup>3</sup> over an 8-hour workday. The <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_for_Occupational_Safety_and_Health" title="National Institute for Occupational Safety and Health">National Institute for Occupational Safety and Health</a> (NIOSH) has set a <a href="/wiki/Recommended_exposure_limit" title="Recommended exposure limit">recommended exposure limit</a> (REL) of 1&#160;mg/m<sup>3</sup> over an 8-hour workday and a short term limit of 3&#160;mg/m<sup>3</sup>. At levels of 500&#160;mg/m<sup>3</sup>, manganese is <a href="/wiki/IDLH" class="mw-redirect" title="IDLH">immediately dangerous to life and health</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Generally, exposure to ambient Mn air concentrations in excess of 5 μg Mn/m3 can lead to Mn-induced symptoms. Increased <a href="/wiki/Ferroportin" title="Ferroportin">ferroportin</a> protein expression in human embryonic kidney (HEK293) cells is associated with decreased intracellular Mn concentration and attenuated <a href="/wiki/Cytotoxicity" title="Cytotoxicity">cytotoxicity</a>, characterized by the reversal of Mn-reduced <a href="/wiki/Glutamate" class="mw-redirect" title="Glutamate">glutamate</a> uptake and diminished <a href="/wiki/Lactate_dehydrogenase" title="Lactate dehydrogenase">lactate dehydrogenase</a> leakage.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_health_concerns">Environmental health concerns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manganese&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Environmental health concerns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manganese_in_drinking_water">Manganese in drinking water</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manganese&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Manganese in drinking water">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Waterborne manganese has a greater <a href="/wiki/Bioavailability" title="Bioavailability">bioavailability</a> than dietary manganese. According to results from a 2010 study,<sup id="cite_ref-Bouchard_138–143_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bouchard_138–143-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> higher levels of exposure to manganese in <a href="/wiki/Drinking_water" title="Drinking water">drinking water</a> are associated with increased <a href="/wiki/Intellectual_impairment" class="mw-redirect" title="Intellectual impairment">intellectual impairment</a> and reduced <a href="/wiki/Intelligence_quotient" title="Intelligence quotient">intelligence quotients</a> in school-age children. It is hypothesized that long-term exposure due to inhaling the naturally occurring manganese in shower water puts up to 8.7 million Americans at risk.<sup id="cite_ref-elsner_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elsner-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> However, data indicates that the human body can recover from certain adverse effects of overexposure to manganese if the exposure is stopped and the body can clear the excess.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manganese_in_gasoline">Manganese in gasoline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manganese&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Manganese in gasoline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:206px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Methylcyclopentadienyl_manganese_tricarbonyl.tif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Methylcyclopentadienyl_manganese_tricarbonyl.tif/lossy-page1-204px-Methylcyclopentadienyl_manganese_tricarbonyl.tif.jpg" width="204" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Methylcyclopentadienyl_manganese_tricarbonyl.tif/lossy-page1-306px-Methylcyclopentadienyl_manganese_tricarbonyl.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Methylcyclopentadienyl_manganese_tricarbonyl.tif/lossy-page1-408px-Methylcyclopentadienyl_manganese_tricarbonyl.tif.jpg 2x" data-file-width="204" data-file-height="151" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Methylcyclopentadienyl_manganese_tricarbonyl.tif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Molecular model of <a href="/wiki/Methylcyclopentadienyl_manganese_tricarbonyl" title="Methylcyclopentadienyl manganese tricarbonyl">methylcyclopentadienyl manganese tricarbonyl</a> (MMT)</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Methylcyclopentadienyl_manganese_tricarbonyl" title="Methylcyclopentadienyl manganese tricarbonyl">Methylcyclopentadienyl manganese tricarbonyl</a> (MMT) is a <a href="/wiki/Gasoline" title="Gasoline">gasoline</a> additive used to replace lead compounds for unleaded gasolines to improve the <a href="/wiki/Octane_rating" title="Octane rating">octane rating</a> of low octane petroleum distillates. It reduces <a href="/wiki/Engine_knocking" title="Engine knocking">engine knock</a> agent through the action of the <a href="/wiki/Carbonyl" class="mw-redirect" title="Carbonyl">carbonyl groups</a>. Fuels containing manganese tend to form manganese carbides, which damage <a href="/wiki/Exhaust_valve" class="mw-redirect" title="Exhaust valve">exhaust valves</a>. The need for lead or manganese additives is merely historic because the modern reformation processes create fuels with increased octane ratings. Such fuels, directly or in mixture with non-reformed distillates, are universal in developed countries (0EU, Japan, etc.). In the US, the imperative to provide the lowest price per volume on motor fuels and the lowest taxation rate, combined with lax legislation of fuel content before the year 2000, encouraged refineries to use MMT. Compared to 1953, levels of manganese in air have dropped.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Many racing competitions specifically ban manganese compounds in racing fuel for carts and minibikes. MMT contains 24.4–25.2% manganese. Elevated atmospheric manganese concentrations are strongly correlated with automobile traffic density.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manganese_in_tobacco_smoke">Manganese in tobacco smoke</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manganese&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Manganese in tobacco smoke">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Tobacco plant">tobacco plant</a> readily absorbs and accumulates <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metals" title="Heavy metals">heavy metals</a> such as manganese from the surrounding soil into its leaves. These are subsequently inhaled during <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_smoking" title="Tobacco smoking">tobacco smoking</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> While  manganese is a constituent of <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_smoke" title="Tobacco smoke">tobacco smoke</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-TalhoutSchulz2011_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TalhoutSchulz2011-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> studies have largely concluded that concentrations are not hazardous for human health.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Role_in_neurological_disorders">Role in neurological disorders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manganese&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Role in neurological disorders">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manganism">Manganism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manganese&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Manganism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Manganism" title="Manganism">Manganism</a></div>
<p>Manganese overexposure is most frequently associated with <a href="/wiki/Manganism" title="Manganism">manganism</a>, a rare neurological disorder associated with excessive manganese ingestion or inhalation. Historically, persons employed in the production or processing of manganese alloys<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> have been at risk for developing manganism; however, current health and safety regulations protect workers in developed nations.<sup id="cite_ref-osha.gov_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osha.gov-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The disorder was first described in 1837 by British academic John Couper, who studied two patients who were manganese grinders.<sup id="cite_ref-Couper_1837_41–42_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Couper_1837_41–42-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Manganism is a biphasic disorder. In its early stages, an intoxicated person may experience depression, mood swings, compulsive behaviors, and psychosis. Early neurological symptoms give way to late-stage manganism, which resembles <a href="/wiki/Parkinson%27s_disease" title="Parkinson&#39;s disease">Parkinson's disease</a>. Symptoms include weakness, monotone and slowed speech, an expressionless face, tremor, forward-leaning gait, inability to walk backwards without falling, rigidity, and general problems with dexterity, gait and balance.<sup id="cite_ref-Couper_1837_41–42_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Couper_1837_41–42-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cersosimo_2007_340–346_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cersosimo_2007_340–346-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Unlike <a href="/wiki/Parkinson%27s_disease" title="Parkinson&#39;s disease">Parkinson's disease</a>, manganism is not associated with loss of the sense of smell and patients are typically unresponsive to treatment with <a href="/wiki/L-DOPA" title="L-DOPA">L-DOPA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Symptoms of late-stage manganism become more severe over time even if the source of exposure is removed and brain manganese levels return to normal.<sup id="cite_ref-Cersosimo_2007_340–346_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cersosimo_2007_340–346-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chronic manganese exposure has been shown to produce a parkinsonism-like illness characterized by movement abnormalities.<sup id="cite_ref-Guilarte2015_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guilarte2015-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> This condition is not responsive to <a href="/wiki/Management_of_Parkinson%27s_disease" title="Management of Parkinson&#39;s disease">typical therapies used in the treatment of PD</a>, suggesting an alternative pathway than the typical <a href="/wiki/Dopamine" title="Dopamine">dopaminergic</a> loss within the <a href="/wiki/Substantia_nigra" title="Substantia nigra">substantia nigra</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guilarte2015_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guilarte2015-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Manganese may accumulate in the <a href="/wiki/Basal_ganglia" title="Basal ganglia">basal ganglia</a>, leading to the abnormal movements.<sup id="cite_ref-Kwakye2015_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kwakye2015-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> A mutation of the SLC30A10 gene, a manganese efflux transporter necessary for decreasing intracellular Mn, has been linked with the development of this Parkinsonism-like disease.<sup id="cite_ref-Peres2016_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peres2016-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Lewy_body" title="Lewy body">Lewy bodies</a> typical to PD are not seen in Mn-induced parkinsonism.<sup id="cite_ref-Kwakye2015_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kwakye2015-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Animal experiments have given the opportunity to examine the consequences of manganese overexposure under controlled conditions. In (non-aggressive) rats, manganese induces mouse-killing behavior.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Childhood_developmental_disorders">Childhood developmental disorders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manganese&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Childhood developmental disorders">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Several recent studies attempt to examine the effects of chronic low-dose manganese overexposure on <a href="/wiki/Child_development" title="Child development">child development</a>. The earliest study was conducted in the Chinese province of Shanxi. Drinking water there had been contaminated through improper sewage irrigation and contained 240–350&#160;µg Mn/L. Although Mn concentrations at or below 300&#160;µg Mn/L were considered safe at the time of the study by the US EPA and 400&#160;µg Mn/L by the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>, the 92 children sampled (between 11 and 13 years of age) from this province displayed lower performance on tests of manual dexterity and rapidity, short-term memory, and visual identification, compared to children from an uncontaminated area. More recently, a study of 10-year-old children in Bangladesh showed a relationship between Mn concentration in well water and diminished IQ scores. A third study conducted in Quebec examined school children between the ages of 6 and 15 living in homes that received water from a well containing 610&#160;µg Mn/L; controls lived in homes that received water from a 160&#160;µg Mn/L well. Children in the experimental group showed increased hyperactive and oppositional behavior.<sup id="cite_ref-Bouchard_138–143_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bouchard_138–143-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The current maximum safe concentration under EPA rules is 50&#160;µg Mn/L.<sup id="cite_ref-EPA_drinking_water_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EPA_drinking_water-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Neurodegenerative_diseases">Neurodegenerative diseases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manganese&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Neurodegenerative diseases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A protein called <a href="/wiki/DMT1" title="DMT1">DMT1</a> is the major transporter in manganese absorption from the intestine, and may be the major transporter of manganese across the <a href="/wiki/Blood%E2%80%93brain_barrier" title="Blood–brain barrier">blood–brain barrier</a>. <a href="/wiki/DMT1" title="DMT1">DMT1</a> also transports inhaled manganese across the nasal epithelium. The proposed mechanism for manganese toxicity is that dysregulation leads to oxidative stress, mitochondrial dysfunction, glutamate-mediated excitoxicity, and aggregation of proteinsc<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>.
</p>
